./.github/workflows/release.yml
name: build-test-publish

on:
  push:
    branches: [ main ]
    tags: [ 'v*' ]

jobs:
  test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        with:
          fetch-depth: 0          # ensure tags are present for dynamic version
      - uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: '3.12'
      - run: python -m pip install --upgrade pip
      - run: python -m pip install -e '.[dev]'
      - run: make test            # pyproject.toml addopts should skip legacy

  publish:
    needs: test
    if: startsWith(github.ref, 'refs/tags/v')
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    permissions:
      id-token: write   # Trusted Publisher
      contents: read
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        with:
          fetch-depth: 0          # CRITICAL for dynamic version from tag
      - uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with:
          python-version: '3.12'
      - run: python -m pip install --upgrade build
      - run: python -m build      # creates dist/*
      - name: Publish to PyPI
        uses: pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish@release/v1

./docs/internal_guide/ai_policy/ai_primer_prompt.adoc
=== AI Primer and Persona Guidelines

==== Introduction

This primer defines how AI assistants, agents, and interactive sessions should act within this project. It establishes shared conventions, coding standards, and communication practices to ensure consistency and reproducibility across all AI-assisted workflows.

A general AI instance (for example, an interactive chat assistant) is expected to follow *all* rules pragmatically and apply the relevant persona-specific guidance when acting in different roles such as Programmer, Requirements Engineer, or Tester.

If a situation is ambiguous, the AI should favor clarity, reproducibility, and safety over brevity or stylistic preference.

**Personas**

AI agents can assume specific roles. Each persona section defines expectations and behavior for that role. Agents primed for a single role should follow the *General* section and their respective persona rules.

**Environments**

Certain instructions act as safeguards specific to an execution context. A repo-committing agent, for example, follows different output conventions than an interactive chat window. The *Environment* sections define these context-specific adaptations.

==== General

===== Purpose and Scope

- Establish a common behavioral baseline for AI participation in this project.
- Define documentation and formatting practices that prevent UI-induced corruption of files.
- Ensure AI-generated artifacts remain deterministic, testable, and reviewable.

===== General Interaction Guidelines

- Prefer clarity and completeness over brevity.
- Be transparent about AI involvement and reasoning sources.
- Prioritize data integrity, reproducibility, and safety in all actions.
- Follow version control conventions; avoid non-deterministic or environment-dependent outputs.

===== Language

* Everything that goes into the repo should be in English unless internationalization is an expressed objective
- code comments
- documentation (functional, technical, project planning)
- variable names (exception: localized business background - e.g. legislation etc.)
* chat interaction with the user can be either in English or the users preferred language.

include::git.adoc[]


=== Personas

==== Persona: Programmer

===== Purpose

Defines expectations for AI agents performing coding, refactoring, or technical design tasks.

===== General Coding Practices

- Follow repository linting and style conventions.
- Produce self-contained code unless context integration is explicitly defined.
- Write minimal inline comments explaining *why*, not *what*.
- Avoid overengineering; prefer composable, testable functions.
- Maintain compatibility with Python >= 3.10.
- Reuse existing modules and architecture patterns (IR, orchestrator, router, passes).

===== Documentation and Code Output

- use ''' for a horizontal line in adoc not ---

===== General Conventions

* Act as a pragmatic senior developer / architect and DevOps specialist.
* Prefer solutions that follow established best practice patterns.
* If something is unclear: ask at most *one* clarifying question, otherwise proceed
with the safest assumption and state it.
* Provide crisp step-by-step instructions with exact shell commands
(`git`, `make`, `pip`, `pytest`) and short explanations.
* Be precise: commands should be copy/paste-ready.
* Anticipate possible error messages and explain how to interpret and fix them.
* Apply **Test Driven Development (TDD)**.
* Minimize external dependencies.
* Code must be robust and run under Linux shell and Windows WSL.
* Major architectural decisions should be captured as ADRs.

===== Testing



===== Artifact Delivery

* Prefer whole files with a heading: `File: <path>` and then the complete file content.
* If only one unit changes:
*“In file `<path>` replace entire function/class `<qualified name>`”* followed by the full unit.
* No diffs/patches or loose snippets requiring manual merging.
* Always runnable code, never pseudo-code.
* Readability is a priority.
* No ambiguous placeholders. Provide safe defaults with clear `TODO` markers.
* Avoid git patches (with + and - and prefer complete blocks or even files to avoid error prone manual processing)

===== Repository / Project structure

* Adhere to best practices
* Advise on structure
* If working over multiple projects - aim for consistency in structure and naming conventions

===== Versioning & Release

* Semantic Versioning with pre-releases (e.g. `v0.1.0b2`).
* Tags follow `v<version>` (e.g. `v1.0.0`).
* Conventional Commits style (`feat:`, `fix:`, `chore:`) recommended.

===== Programming Language–Specific Conventions

====== Python

- At least all public functions and methods require type hints.
- use _future_ annotations
- Use dataclasses where suitable; prefer immutability unless mutation is domain-relevant.
- Prefer composition over inheritance except for ABCs or explicit extension points.
- Follow Python naming conventions:
* `lowercase_with_underscores` for functions and variables.
* `PascalCase` for classes.
* `UPPERCASE` for constants.
- Apply **Coverage Reporting** (`pytest-cov`), and point out coverage gaps.

====== Makefile

* Provide entire targets when modified (or the full file if multiple targets change).

NOTE: Multi-line shell logic inside Make recipes (especially with if, then, else, and \ continuations) often breaks because Make, /bin/sh, and Bash each perform their own quoting and line-parsing.

* To avoid these “Makefile-Bash interference” issues and ensure predictable behavior, externalize complex procedural logic into standalone scripts outside the Makefile (e.g., `tools/ensure_pip.sh`) that are invoked as single-line commands from the Makefile.

====== Bash

* Use strict mode: `set -euo pipefail` to enforce fail-fast execution.
* Prefer Python for complex logic (better testability/readability).
* Keep scripts POSIX-compatible unless Bash-specific behavior is intentional.
* Document environment variables at the top of each script.
* For complex logic (better testability/readability) consider alternatives e.g. Python and propose them to the user.

====== YAML / JSON Configurations

- Validate syntax before committing; use consistent indentation (2 spaces for YAML).
- Use explicit booleans (`true`/`false`) and avoid `null` unless required.
- Comment configuration keys with expected data types and semantics.

==== Persona: Requirements Engineer

===== Purpose

Defines how AI agents should analyze requirements and translate business needs into structured technical specifications.

===== Practices

- Express requirements as *testable behaviors*, not vague intentions.
- Maintain traceability between requirements and FTR (Feature) entries.
- Use consistent terminology: *Feature*, *Epic*, *Acceptance Criteria*.
- When converting informal goals into backlog entries, include *Purpose*, *Scope*, *Solution*, and *Acceptance* sections.
- Respect AsciiDoc heading levels to preserve structural clarity.

===== Documentation Conventions

- Avoid duplication; cross-reference related features with `<<filename.adoc#,FTR-ID>>`.
- Write concise, active sentences; use imperative voice for acceptance criteria.

==== Persona: Tester, Test Developer

===== Purpose

Outlines expectations for AI agents designing, maintaining, or analyzing test suites.

===== Testing Principles

* Target full coverage of critical paths; clarity outweighs assertion density.
* Use realistic input data and ensure deterministic tests.
* Verify correctness and reproducibility (identical inputs → identical outputs).
* Distinguish *unit*, *integration*, and *system* tests using naming and markers.
* Tests must be hermetic and fast (no network).
* Use the filesystem only if the purpose of the test is IO.

===== Output Conventions

- Test code follows Programmer output rules: fenced code blocks with `python` tags.
- Begin each test file or suite with a short docstring describing its purpose.
- Use AsciiDoc tables (wrapped in JSON lists when required) to present datasets or expected results clearly.

==== Persona: Documentation Writer

===== Purpose

Guides AI agents producing or maintaining documentation within the repository.

===== Practices

- Keep documentation modular; prefer small files included via `include::[]`.
- Maintain consistent heading hierarchy: `==` for chapters, `===` for sections, etc.
- Use English for all repository-facing documentation.
- Apply `NOTE`, `TIP`, `WARNING`, and `CAUTION` blocks to highlight key information.
- Prefer internal cross-references to external links.

==== Persona: Architect (Placeholder)

Reserved for future specialization in system-level design, crosscutting decisions, and architectural reasoning. Until defined, follow both *Programmer* and *Requirements Engineer* guidelines.

==== Persona: Project Manager (Placeholder)

Defines behavior for coordination, planning, and progress tracking tasks. To be detailed once automated workflow or reporting agents are introduced.

=== Environments

==== Environment: Interactive UIs (e.g., ChatGPT Web Interface)

===== Output rule for files containing characters that may conflict with UI rendering (AsciiDoc, Markdown, etc.)

When asked to produce a file, place the entire file content inside a fenced code block, ensuring literal text output. Within that fenced block, emit the file as a JSON list of strings, one line per list element.

Do not include any explanatory text *inside* the fenced block. Notes or explanations may appear *outside* the block, before or after it.

Example:

----
Here’s the generated AsciiDoc file:

```
[
"== Example",
"",
"This text includes a fenced code sample:",
"```python",
"a = 1",
"b = 2",
"print(a < b)",
"```"
]
```
----

This method preserves underscores, asterisks, and backticks that interactive UIs may misinterpret as formatting. It also maintains compatibility with extraction scripts such as `jq`.

===== Handling Quotes in JSON

If the output requires quotation marks, escape them inside JSON strings using `\"`. Example:

```
[
"This line contains a \"quoted string\" that will render correctly."
]
```

Using `jq -r '.[]'` unescapes these characters, producing a valid literal file.

===== Motivation

Interactive chat interfaces render AsciiDoc and Markdown as formatted text, potentially corrupting source syntax. The JSON-in-code-block format acts as a protective shell, ensuring that generated documentation remains literal and machine-extractable.

To produce the final file from such JSON output, use:

-----
cat input.json | jq -r '.[]' > output.adoc
-----

===== Scope

- Applies to human-readable documentation (AsciiDoc, Markdown, RST, plaintext).
- Not applicable to executable formats (Python, YAML, Shell, JSON schema). These use normal fenced code blocks without JSON.

==== Environment: Repo-Committing Agent (Future)

Agents committing directly to the repository or file system should emit files as plain text or structured code without JSON wrapping. The JSON-wrapping rule is unnecessary here and may interfere with automation pipelines.

==== Environment: CLI / Batch Mode (Placeholder)

Defines interaction style and safety guidelines for agents running locally or via CI/CD. To be extended once command-line automation or build integration is introduced.

===== Git Primer (Project Standards)

====== Commit Message Conventions
* Follow Conventional Commits: `type(scope): summary`
* Use the FTR ID as the scope (e.g., `feat(FTR-IR-WRITEPATH-P1): ...`)
* Keep subjects ≤ 72 chars, body optional but encouraged for rationale.
* One logical change per commit.
* Reference GitHub issues or discussions in the footer if relevant.

====== Branching & Merge Policy
* Use feature branches for code-bearing work; docs-only changes may go directly to `dev`.
* Maintain a `main` (stable) and `dev` (integration) branch.
* Prefer **rebase merges** to keep history linear.
* Rebase your branch on `dev` before opening a PR or merge request.
* Use signed tags for releases.

=== Project Specific Conventions

These conventions are relevant for both AI (in the sense of a primer) and for human collaborators

==== related Repositories

* *spreadsheet-handling* — core tool, published on PyPI under MIT, hosted on GitHub.
* *spreadsheet-handling-demo* — educational usage and plugin examples, hosted on GitHub.

The demo and company repos consume the package from *spreadsheet-handling*.
Repository structures should remain aligned where possible.

==== Technology Choices

* **Language:** Python ≥ 3.10.
* **Docs/Comments:** English. Chat can be in English or German.
* **Tools:** `make`, `ruff`, `black`, `pytest`, `pytest-cov`, `compileall` for syntax.
* **Build Backend:** setuptools + setuptools-scm (no Hatchling).

==== CI/CD

* Public: GitHub Actions.
* Company: GitLab CI.
* Pipeline stages: lint → syntax → tests (+coverage) → build sdist/wheel → publish on tags.

==== Respect Project Conventions

* Follow existing Makefile and env patterns.
* Ensure commands work on Linux and WSL (watch path quoting).

==== Testing

* Prefer small, in-memory DataFrames; assert schema, row count, and keys explicitly.

=== AI Transparency Note

*Principles*

- AI tools are used at all levels of this project: requirement analysis, solution design, coding.
- Human oversight, testing, and review remain essential. AI augments reasoning and speed but does not replace engineering judgment.
- Quality and maintainability are goals treated with priority; AI contributes to these.

*Industry trends support this approach:*
according to the https://www.golem.de/news/umfrage-unter-24-000-entwicklern-gesamtes-berufsfeld-befindet-sich-im-wandel-2510-188855.html[JetBrains Developer Ecosystem 2025 survey published by *Golem.de*], AI adoption is already pervasive and considered a core competency by now contradicting earlier concerns that AI use compromises code quality.

*Consequences*

- The repo should be AI friendly in the sense that it also explicitly holds the context necessary for continuing development with AI in a new context window.
- Our user documentation should follow that spirit to and allow the user to use AI easily for instance to generate the required yaml files../docs/internal_guide/ai_policy/_ai_policy.adoc

=== ARCH-LAYERS — Layer Responsibilities and Boundaries

:updated: 2025-10-28
:status:

This section defines the conceptual layers of the Spreadsheet Handling architecture and their relationships.
It clarifies boundaries, dependencies, and responsibilities to ensure modularity and avoid leakage between concerns.

The layering follows a clean/hexagonal architecture mindset, with *CLI* and *I/O backends* as ports,
and *Pipeline*, *Domain*, and *Render IR* as the inner structure.

'''

==== 1) CLI Layer — Input Port

*Role:*
User- and system-facing entry point. This layer defines how the system is invoked, configured, and orchestrated from the outside.

*Responsibilities:*
- Provide a unified command-line interface (`sh` tool / `cli.py`).
- Collect configuration, input sources, and command arguments.
- Delegate execution to the **Pipeline** layer.
- Handle exit codes, logging, diagnostics, and global error handling.
- Never contain business logic or transformation rules.

*Must NOT:*
- Perform domain transformations.
- Contain serialization or deserialization logic for workbooks.
- Reference concrete I/O backends.

*Dependencies:*
→ Pipeline layer (calls into it)
← none

'''

==== 2) PIPELINE Layer — Application / Orchestration Layer

*Role:*
Coordinates the high-level workflow. In DDD terms, this is the **Application Service Layer**.
It wires together domain operations, rendering, and persistence without embedding business rules.

*Responsibilities:*

- Execute user-defined or system-defined sequences of transformations (domain pipelines).
- Manage lifecycle and context for transformations (e.g., staging, logging, metrics).
- Orchestrate calls into the **Domain** layer and downstream into **Render IR** or other output ports.
- Maintain order and dependency of tasks; assemble results and errors.

*Must NOT:*

- Contain domain-specific logic (e.g., how a transformation computes its output).
- Embed rendering or backend-specific logic.

*Dependencies:*

* Domain (to execute transformations)
* Render IR (for spreadsheet persistence)
* Directly to other I/O backends (for non-spreadsheet formats like JSON, CSV, XML)

'''

==== 3) DOMAIN Layer — Core Model and Business Logic

*Role:*::
The heart of the system. Holds all business rules, transformation semantics, and validation logic.

*Responsibilities:*

- Define the **Domain Model**: workbook, worksheet, and transformation objects.
- Implement domain transformations (`Workbook → Workbook`).
- Produce **semantic meta-information** that describes the workbook (e.g., which columns are ephemeral, linked, calculated, foreign keys, or required).
- Guarantee deterministic results for equivalent inputs.
- Contain all invariants and validation rules.

*Must NOT:*

- Reference user interface or CLI.
- Reference spreadsheet libraries, OpenPyXL, or other persistence details.
- Know about file formats or concrete renderers.

*Dependencies:*

→ none (pure core)
← Pipeline orchestrates it.

'''

==== 4) RENDER IR Layer — Rendering Abstraction / Spreadsheet Adapter

*Role:*::
Adapter layer for spreadsheet-like backends (XLSX, ODS, OOXML).
It translates domain results and meta-information into **backend-agnostic layout directives** (RenderPlan).
This layer exists to avoid duplicating spreadsheet-specific logic across different backends.

*Responsibilities:*::
- Convert Domain Workbook + Meta into **RenderPlan** (abstract representation of layout directives).
- Express universal spreadsheet concepts: headers, filters, validations, named ranges, freeze panes, merges, styles, formula directives.
- Provide passes (RenderPasses) to enrich and normalize the RenderPlan.
- Define and maintain the **Render IR model** (WorkbookIR, SheetIR, TableBlock, DataValidationSpec, etc.).
- Ensure backend-agnostic semantics.

*Must NOT:*::
- Import or reference backend APIs (OpenPyXL, odfpy, etc.).
- Write files or manage serialization formats.
- Duplicate logic that belongs to domain transformations.

*Output:*::
- **RenderPlan** (sequence of RenderOps).
  Examples: `DefineSheet`, `SetHeader`, `ApplyHeaderStyle`, `SetAutoFilter`, `AddValidation`, `MergeCells`, `WriteMeta`.

*Dependencies:*::
→ I/O Backend (via protocol or adapter)
← Pipeline invokes it.

'''
==== 5) IO_BACKEND Layer — Output Port / Technical Persistence

*Role:*
Implements concrete persistence adapters (e.g., `.xlsx`, `.ods`, `.csv`, `.json`, `.yaml`, `.xml`).
Each backend converts abstract render or data directives into a specific file format or stream.

*Responsibilities:*
- Implement a protocol interface (e.g., `XlsxBackend.render(plan: RenderPlan, path: str)`).
- Map RenderOps to concrete APIs (OpenPyXL, odfpy, csv, JSON dumpers).
- Handle format quirks (shared strings, zip ordering, themes, data validation syntax).
- Guarantee deterministic output and normalization for tests.
- Provide backend-specific regression tests.

*Must NOT:*
- Reinterpret or change semantic meaning of RenderOps.
- Contain domain logic.
- Expose backend-specific types to upper layers.

*Dependencies:*
→ External libraries (OpenPyXL, odfpy, Python stdlib)
← Invoked by Render IR for spreadsheet outputs or by Pipeline for simpler formats (CSV, JSON, YAML).

'''

==== Layer Dependency Overview

./docs/internal_guide/architecture/_architecture.adoc
== Architecture items

include::ARCH-LAYERS.adoc[]./docs/internal_guide/architecture_decision_records/adr-001_hexagonal_architecture.adoc
=== ADR-001 — Hexagonal Architecture (Pragmatic Adoption)

**Status:** Accepted

**Context**::
* The `spreadsheet-handling` library should remain modular while keeping overall complexity manageable.
* A classic hexagonal (ports-and-adapters) architecture cleanly separates domain, infrastructure, and I/O layers.
* Python, however is not suitable for a literal adoption:
  ** lack of strict typing
  ** no formal interfaces, no dependency injection containers
  ** no concept of private access

**Decision**::
* Adopt the *principle* of the hexagonal architecture with a great deal of pragmatism:
  ** No mapping between layers:  (Our home brew `meta` and `Panda` 's `DataFrame` type are used outside the "domain" layer)
  ** Minimal ports: In the absence of formal interfaces or DI containers our adapters only implement a tiny surface ('read_multi', 'write_multi').
  ** No type safety: We use a simple dictionary for 'meta' instead of a schema
  ** Strong coupling between domain and adapter layer: 'meta' is encoded by the domain and interpreted by the adapter.

* Each adapter exposes a pragmatic, minimal interface (`read_multi`, `write_multi`).
* Focus on exchangeability and testability, not on formal interface purity.

**Consequences**::
* Structural clarity and replaceability are preserved.
* Complexity remains low compared with a fully abstract implementation.
* Some coupling (e.g., use of Pandas DataFrames inside the domain) is accepted as pragmatic compromise../docs/internal_guide/architecture_decision_records/adr-002_pandas.adoc
=== ADR-002 — Pandas as Core Data Representation

**Status:** Accepted

**Context**::
A theoretically 'pure' domain would avoid depending on Pandas and define its own entities and value objects.
In practice, nearly every layer of the system—domain logic, transformations, validations, and adapters—relies on Pandas DataFrames.

**Decision**::
- Pandas is accepted as part of the *domain model*.
- DataFrames are the shared representation between all layers (domain, transformations, rendering, I/O).
- No artificial abstraction is added as long as Pandas meets the requirements.

**Consequences**::
- High productivity and compatibility with the Python data ecosystem.
- Loss of theoretical domain purity (domain ≠ library-independent).
- Replacing Pandas in the future would be costly but this is accepted due to the ubiquity of the lib../docs/internal_guide/architecture_decision_records/adr-003_intermediate_representation_layer.adoc
=== ADR-003 — Intermediate Representation (IR) Layer for Spreadsheet Rendering

**Status:** Accepted

**Context**::
Multiple spreadsheet adapters (XLSX, ODS) share similar logic for layout, styling, validation, and metadata persistence.
Adapters dedicated to a simple serialization format (JSON, YAML, XML) however do not require this logic.
Duplicating this logic in every adapter would lead to divergence and maintenance overhead.

**Decision**::
- Introduce a shared *Intermediate Representation (IR)* layer responsible for rendering spreadsheets.
- The domain produces `frames + meta`; the IR layer handles layout, styling, validations, and meta persistence.
- Only spreadsheet-type backends (XLSX, ODS) use this layer; JSON/YAML backends bypass it entirely.

**Consequences**::
- Rendering logic is centralized and extensible via passes (StylePass, ValidationPass, FormulaPass, MetaPass, etc.).
- Spreadsheet adapters become smaller, simpler, and easier to maintain.
- Non-spreadsheet formats remain lightweight and unaffected by presentation concerns../docs/internal_guide/architecture_decision_records/adr-004_meta.adoc
=== ADR-004 — Meta as Persistent and Mergeable Configuration

**Status:** Accepted

**Context**::
Meta information controls many behavioral aspects: styling, validations, compact mappings, and heuristics.
Initially, meta data was implicit in code or passed through the CLI configuration.
As complexity grew, a unified and persistable source of truth became necessary.

**Decision**::
- Meta is treated as a first-class entity (a structured dictionary) existing both in runtime and persisted artifacts.
- Missing meta is treated as an empty `{}` (fault-tolerant).
- Spreadsheet formats persist meta in a hidden sheet (`_meta`); JSON/YAML may embed it inline or as a sidecar file.
- Early in the pipeline, a dedicated transformation `bootstrap_meta` injects configuration defaults into meta.
- Merge priority: (1) Runtime Config → (2) Persisted Meta → (3) Heuristics/Defaults.

**Consequences**::
- Clear distinction between transient configuration (CLI) and persisted metadata (artifact).
- All backends tolerate missing meta gracefully.
- Deterministic merge behavior and unit-testable precedence rules.
- Provides a consistent foundation for style, validation, and transformation features../docs/internal_guide/architecture_decision_records/adr-005.adoc
=== ADR-005 — Dual Test Harness (Legacy vs. IR)

**Status:** Accepted

**Context**::
During the migration from the legacy XLSX backend to the new IR-based renderer, both variants must coexist safely within CI pipelines.

**Decision**::
- Introduce two explicit Pytest markers:
* `@pytest.mark.xlsx_ir` — tests that target the new IR-based backend.
* `@pytest.mark.xlsx_legacy` — tests that validate the legacy behavior.
- Extend Makefile with dedicated targets:
* `make test` — default suite (excludes both legacy and IR-only tests).
* `make test-ir` — runs IR-specific tests (`-m xlsx_ir`, `--ignore=tests/legacy`).
* `make test-legacy` — runs legacy tests (`-m xlsx_legacy`).
- Add environment variable `SH_XLSX_BACKEND` to control the active backend (`legacy` | `ir` | `auto`).

**Consequences**::
- Safe parallel execution of both backends with isolated markers.
- CI/CD pipelines remain stable throughout migration.
- Developers can incrementally retag tests once feature parity is reached.
- Simplifies rollout, regression testing, and code review processes../docs/internal_guide/architecture_decision_records/ADR-RENDER-FLOW-VS-DOMAIN-PIPELINE.adoc
=== ADR-RENDER-FLOW-VS-DOMAIN-PIPELINE: Terminologie & Trennung — Domain „Pipeline“ vs. IR „Render-Flow“

:date: 2025-10-28
:deciders: dr_stefan_schade@yahoo.com

==== Context
The term “pipeline” is established for the domain transformation flow. The IR/XLSX path also used “pipeline”, which risks ambiguity across layers. A unifying abstraction was considered but the responsibilities (inputs/outputs, invariants, error models, performance) differ substantially.

==== Decision
Use **“Pipeline”** exclusively for the **Domain** layer, and **“Render-Flow”** for the **IR/Rendering** layer. Do not introduce an abstraction that unifies both.

Renames (IR layer):
- Functions: `compose` → `compose_ir`, `run_passes` → `apply_ir_passes`, `render` → `render_xlsx`
- Files: `rendering/pipeline.py` → `rendering/flow.py`; `rendering/passes/p1_core.py` → `rendering/passes/core.py`
- Add a glossary distinction in documentation.

==== Alternatives Considered
. Single abstract “Pipeline” interface across layers — *Rejected.* Would create leaky abstractions and coupling.
. Keep “pipeline” in both layers — *Rejected.* Leads to confusion in PRs, onboarding, docs.

==== Rationale
Clear terminology reduces review friction and aids debugging (stack traces reflect the layer). It keeps domain evolution decoupled from rendering and vice versa.

==== Consequences
- Small refactors (names/imports) without runtime behavior changes.
- Docs and roadmap wording updated (use “Render-Flow”).

=== Early Project Evolution

Before starting to track via the backlog presented in this section we first relied on GitHub' s ticketing system for a while and then worked without strict ties to tickets for a while. This seemed pragmatic at the time but it obscures the purpose of the early commits. This brief section recounts the origin of the project history. For deep dives, read commit messages linked above and the section on **Concepts**.

*2025-08–09 — Proof of Concept & Early Structure*

- First JSON↔Spreadsheet transforms;
- tests and robustness passes.

*2025-09-02…09 — Modularization & Multi-backend groundwork*

- Modularize conversion logic;
- non-XLS backends start;
- README and repo structuring.

*2025-09-19 — Pipeline primitives*
- Introduce `BoundStep` and `run_pipeline`
- YAML-defined pipelines
- backend/config tidy
- merge pipeline refactor to `dev`.

*2025-10-01 — Hexagonal redesign milestone*

- Router (get_loader/get_saver), config shim, consistent `read/write_multi`, tests green.
- `pipeline/config.py`, `pipeline/runner.py`, `pipeline/types.py` added.

./docs/internal_guide/backlog/epics.adoc
===  Epics

==== Phase 1 — Stabilize and Modularize the XLSX Backend

*Goal:*::
Separate spreadsheet logic into clear, testable layers without changing existing behavior.

*Key results:*::

- Move all XLSX-specific code into `io_backends/xlsx/` package.
- Introduce the IR (Intermediate Representation) layer with `compose → passes → render` flow.
- Migrate and tag all tests to support `@pytest.mark.xlsx_ir` and `@pytest.mark.xlsx_legacy` dual harness.
- Ensure green CI across both backends.

*Definition of done:* XLSX adapter runs through the IR path; all legacy tests pass or are explicitly tagged; internal APIs stable enough for new features.

==== Phase 2 — Domain Consistency and Meta Integration

*Goal:*::
Establish a unified domain/meta contract shared between CLI, pipeline, and I/O layers.

*Key results:*::

- Introduce `bootstrap_meta` transformation to inject CLI/pipeline config into runtime meta.
- Standardize fault-tolerant meta handling (empty `{}` treated as valid).
- Ensure meta persistence and rehydration across all backends.
- Document and test merge priorities (runtime > persisted > heuristics).

*Definition of done:*::
All adapters and domain transformations can operate without explicit meta; missing metadata never causes failure; roundtrip preserves meta content.

==== Phase 3 — Functional Parity and IR-driven Features

*Goal:*::
Achieve feature parity between the new IR backend and the legacy Excel path while enabling extensible rendering logic.

*Key results:*::

- Move validation, style, and formula logic into dedicated IR passes (`ValidationPass`, `StylePass`, etc.).
- Re-implement complex behaviors (multi-sheet layouts, hidden meta sheets, data validation lists).
- Use IR tests to confirm parity with legacy outputs for known examples.
- Provide extension hooks for future custom passes (e.g., domain-specific formatting).

*Definition of done:*::
IR backend produces visually and semantically equivalent workbooks for all core scenarios; legacy path officially deprecated in CI.

==== Phase 4 — Feature Expansion and Domain Transformations

*Goal:*::
Introduce new transformation capabilities and richer domain logic leveraging the stable IR and meta foundation.

*Key results:*::

- Implement `FTR-COMPACT-TRANSFORMS` (cross-table ↔ compact-table bijection).
- Implement `FTR-PARTITION-BY-DOMAIN` (partitioning by component attribute).
- Extend helper-column logic to support multiple enriched columns (name, category, description).
- Improve style/validation passes to handle these structures correctly.

*Definition of done:*::
Transformations are reusable and bijective; IR supports expanded layouts; new tests demonstrate composability of passes and transformations.

==== Phase 5 — Integration and Demonstration (Demo Repository)

*Goal:*::
Connect the refactored core library to the `spreadsheet-handling-demo` repository to demonstrate production usage patterns.

*Key results:*::

* Integrate new IR backend in the demo pipelines and CLI shims.
* Provide example datasets (e.g., product/feature matrix) exercising cross-table and compact transformations.
* Verify JSON ↔ Excel ↔ JSON roundtrip with persisted meta and formatting.
* Document all example workflows in the User and Developer Guides.

*Definition of done:*::
Demo repository runs fully on refactored library; examples reflect all core features; public-facing documentation is aligned and reproducible.

==== Phase 6 — Consolidate Domain

*Goal:*::
delivers higher-level domain features (compact transforms) and schema consolidation.

*Key results:*::

* ....

*Definition of done:*::

* ....


==== Phase 7 — Make final product robust towards 1.0 Release

*Goal:*

* **Cross-cutting** items (perf limits) will be applied where relevant during implementation.
* Final Polish towards Repository and tooling setup
  ** makefile
  ** pytest markers
  ** documentation
  ** CICD pipeline

*Goal:*::
delivers higher-level domain features (compact transforms) and schema consolidation.

===== FTR-TEST-HARNESS — Dual-backend markers & CI targets

* `@pytest.mark.xlsx_ir` and `@pytest.mark.xlsx_legacy`; Make targets `test-ir`, `test-legacy`, default excludes IR-only.
* Acceptance: CI can run legacy-only, IR-only, and full suites; flakes eliminated.
* “Introduce @pytest.mark.xlsx_ir and @pytest.mark.xlsx_legacy; add make test-ir → -m xlsx_ir and make test-legacy → -m xlsx_legacy; document that default make test runs not legacy.” (Matches what’s already half-there.)

**current state in the code**::

**What’s in code now:**::
a solid, fast test runner setup with default marker filtering and convenience targets (test, test-verbose, test-one, test-integ, test-all). Legacy tests are excluded by default via MARK_EXPR=not legacy plus --ignore=tests/legacy when applicable.

**What’s not present:**::
I can’t find the explicit dual markers @pytest.mark.xlsx_ir / @pytest.mark.xlsx_legacy, nor dedicated make test-ir / make test-legacy targets that switch on those markers. The acceptance text for FTR-TEST-HARNESS mentions those specifically, but they aren’t in the code I see.

**Partially done:**::
(runner + legacy filtering are there) but not fully “Done” per the feature’s acceptance (missing the xlsx_ir/xlsx_legacy markers and matching make targets).


*Adjustment of Acceptance Criteria:*

_Purpose:_ Run fast, focused test slices without accidental interference; keep historical tests quarantined.

*Why this is better now*

* Reflects IR as the primary path (so regressions don’t get masked).
* Preserves a clean way to isolate IR or legacy-writer behavior when you need it.
* Keeps the pre-hex suite as documentation/requirements without breaking day-to-day runs.

*We don’t need to “fulfill by the letter” that default excludes IR-only bit anymore.*

*Acceptance:*::
* Default make test runs unit+integration including IR tests, while excluding pre-hex (tests/legacy_pre_hex) by default.
* `@pytest.mark.xlsx_ir` is applied to IR-specific tests; `make test-ir` runs only these.
* If applicable, `@pytest.mark.xlsx_legacy` marks adapter legacy-writer tests; `make test-legacy` runs only these.
* Pre-hex archive remains under `tests/legacy_pre_hex`, marked legacy, ignored by default; optional `make test-prehex` (guarded) exists.
* CI has jobs (or a matrix) for:
  ** unit-fast (default slice),
  ** ir (`test-ir`),
  ** legacy-writer (`test-legacy`, if that path still exists),
  ** (optional scheduled) prehex (`test-prehex`).
  ** Developer help is discoverable (`make help` lists all test targets with descriptions).

*Non-goals:* Forcing IR exclusion by default; running pre-hex tests on every PR../docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/done/_ftrs_done.adoc

===== FTR-DISTRIBUTION-PEX — Self-contained CLI runner for non-developer users

** *Purpose:*  Deliver a single executable (`.pex` / `.pyz`) of spreadsheet-handling for analysts without Python installs.

** *Scope:*  Applies to CLI tools (`sheets-run`, `sheets-pack`, `sheets-unpack`).

** *Solution:*
- Add a Make target and CI job building a PEX or shiv archive from the current wheel.
- Embed version info and reproducible hash for traceability.
- Provide a short usage note for analysts (Windows/macOS/Linux).

** *Acceptance:*
- CI produces `dist/sheets-run.pex` on release tags.
- Analysts can execute it without prior setup; output identical to CLI invocation.
- Docs include 1-page distribution guide.

** *Epic:*  Phase 5 — Distribution & packaging
./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/future/FTR-EXCEL-ADDIN.adoc
===== FTR-EXCEL-ADDIN — In-sheet buttons to trigger processing

** *Purpose:*  Let analysts run pack/unpack or custom pipelines from Excel via ribbon/buttons, avoiding shell/Make usage.

** *Scope:*  Excel-only convenience layer that shells out to the installed runner (CLI or `.pex`). No new business logic.

** *Solution:*
- Provide a minimal add-in approach (choose one):
  - **VBA + shell**: Ribbon button calls a signed VBA macro that executes the local runner with a selected profile.
  - **xlwings** (Python-backed): Button triggers a small Python bridge that calls `orchestrate(...)`.
- Add a sample workbook template (`/examples/excel-runner-template.xlsx`) with the button wired.
- Document how to point the button to profiles/pipelines (per-file or per-folder).

** *Acceptance:*
- Clicking the button runs a demo pipeline and updates/exports artifacts as expected.
- Works on a stock Windows Excel environment without requiring dev tools.
- Template + short setup guide included; simple smoke test in CI (headless where possible).

** *Epic:*  Phase 7 — Future

** *Notes:*  Prefer the simplest path first (VBA + shell to `.pex`) to minimize dependencies; add xlwings later if needed.
./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/future/FTR-WEB-SERVICE.adoc
===== FTR-WEB-SERVICE — FastAPI front-end and optional static UI

** *Purpose:*  Provide an HTTP API (and optional lightweight UI) as an alternative ingress to the CLI, so analysts or other systems can submit jobs without local setup.

** *Scope:*  New process alongside the CLI. Reuses the shared `orchestrate(...)` engine; no business logic in controllers.

** *Solution:*
- Implement a small FastAPI app exposing endpoints:
  - `POST /run`  — accepts profile/pipeline + I/O descriptors (paths/URIs).
  - `GET  /status/{job_id}` — job state/logs (if async mode is added).
  - `GET  /healthz` — readiness probe.
- Add a minimal static client (optional): single-page form that calls `/run`.
- Package service with uvicorn and a Dockerfile for easy deployment.

** *Acceptance:*
- `POST /run` triggers the same path as `sheets-run` and returns results/artifacts or a job id.
- Unit tests for request validation; integration test that compares CLI vs API outputs for a sample pipeline.
- Service can be run locally (`uvicorn app:app`) and via Docker.

** *Epic:*  Phase 7 — Future

** *Notes:*  Keep the API thin; all orchestration stays in the core. Consider auth later if exposed beyond local use.

all done by now./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-ADAPTER-DEPRECATION-STUBS.adoc
===== FTR-ADAPTER-DEPRECATION-STUBS — Quarantine legacy adapters behind clear stubs

*Purpose:*::
Remove dead/obsolete adapter code and replace with minimal stubs that fail fast with actionable messages, reducing maintenance and drift.

*Scope:*::
Affects legacy adapters that are no longer exercised in tests or docs. Only keep router registration + thin stubs.

*Solution:*

- Inventory adapters and tag each as active|deprecated.
- Move deprecated implementations to `adapters/_legacy/` (or delete) and register **stubs** in the router that raise a typed exception with guidance (e.g., `NotImplementedAdapterError(adapter='xml', hint='use json/xlsx or enable new IR path')`).
- Keep adapter-facing **interfaces** stable to avoid ripple effects.
- Update docs to list supported adapters and show deprecation message text.

*Acceptance:*

- All deprecated adapters resolve to stubs that error deterministically with a helpful hint.
- Test suite includes one smoke test per stubbed adapter asserting the error contract.
- CI disallows references to removed modules (import checks).
- Docs reflect the supported set; examples don’t rely on removed code../docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-AUTORELEASE-POLICY.adoc
===== FTR-AUTORELEASE-POLICY — Conservative library, aggressive demo automation

*Purpose:*::
Minimize maintenance while avoiding silent breakage.

*Policy:*

- Demo: Dependabot/ Renovate on PyPI; automerge lib bumps if demo CI:: smoke pass.
- Library: Automerge only dev-tool patch bumps; no automerge for runtime deps or feature PRs.
- Release flow: tag RC → publish to TestPyPI → run full + demo smoke → manual promote tag to PyPI.
- Use `constraints.txt` for runtime pins; demo pins lib with `==`.

*Acceptance:*

- CI workflows exist for RC→TestPyPI and promote-to-PyPI.
- Demo auto-updates itself on new PyPI releases and merges when smoke passes.
- Library never publishes to PyPI without the manual promote step.
./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-BACKEND-ABC.adoc
===== FTR-BACKEND-ABC — Formal backend interface + Table protocol

*Purpose:*::
Provide a stable contract for adapters and catch interface drift via type checking.

*Solution:*

- Convert `BackendBase` to `ABC` with `@abstractmethod read()/write()` and default `read_multi()/write_multi()` loops.
- Introduce a minimal `Table` Protocol (pandas DataFrame conforms).
- Wrap YAML/CSV helpers into `YAMLBackend` / `CSVBackend` thin classes.

*Acceptance:*

- All active adapters subclass `BackendBase` and pass type checks.
- Tests can use a fake backend implementing the ABC/Protocol.
- No behavior change to existing pipelines.
./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-CLEANUP-IR-P4.adoc
===== FTR-CLEANUP-IR-P4 — Remove Legacy Renderer and Parity Safeguard

*Context*::
With parity proven in CI, dual-path support and the temporary safeguard must be removed to minimize complexity and maintenance cost.

*Goal*::
Make the IR renderer the **sole** XLSX path; remove legacy code, flags, Make targets, and the parity CI job. Convert parity fixtures to IR-only golden tests.

*Rationale*::
Eliminates conditional branches, reduces surface for regressions, and simplifies releases and future feature work.

*Acceptance*::
* Adapters and entrypoints use the IR renderer **unconditionally** (no env flags, no runtime switches).
* Legacy OpenPyXL write path and all toggles (e.g., `SH_XLSX_BACKEND`, `--legacy-xlsx`) are **deleted**, including Make targets and dead code.
* The **parity-ir** job is removed. Parity fixtures are retained as **golden snapshot tests (IR-only)** using normalized comparisons (structure/styles/validations/meta).
* `docs/legacy_gap.md` is closed: every item either implemented or explicitly deprecated with rationale.
* Release notes state: **“Legacy OpenPyXL path removed; IR renderer is now the sole backend.”**
* CI is green across the supported matrix with IR-only.

*NOTE:* Forward-only strategy (beta). No runtime fallback remains after P4. A temporary rollback branch/tag may exist outside `main` purely for emergency hotfixes, but it is **not** part of the supported code path.

IMPORTANT: After this is done, no remainder (also no safeguard) should remain from the legacy backend

*Context:*

* Slice P4 of the Roadmap towards IR Parity <<RM-IR-PARITY: Parity between IR renderer and legacy renderer, RM-IR-PARITY>>
* Has to be done at least 5 days after <<./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-COMPACT-TRANSFORMS.adoc
===== FTR-COMPACT-TRANSFORMS — Xref ↔ Cross-table ↔ Compact string (E-V-Z) (bijective)

*Context:*::
We need a reversible mapping between multiple layered cross-tables and a single compact encoding (codes + separator).

*Goal:*::
Implement `contract_compact` (merge n cross-tables → compact) and `expand_compact` (compact → n cross-tables/tuples) as bijective pair.

*Rationale:*::
Enables human-compact views in Excel while retaining machine-friendly long/xref structures.

*Solution Steps:*::

Provide two bijective steps:

. xref⇄cross-table;
. stack multiple cross-tables into compact codes using per-table code + separator.

*Acceptance*

- Configurable `compact_maps` (code ↔ source), separator, and 2- vs. 3-tuple handling.
- Deterministic code ordering and validation list generation (with cap).
- Bijectivity tests for `expand(contract(X)) == X` and vice versa.
- lossless roundtrip across all three forms; separator + mapping fully meta-driven.
./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-CROSSTAB-XREF-LONG.adoc
===== FTR-CROSSTAB-XREF-LONG - Crosstab → XRef (Long-Form) Transformation

*Context*::
Business matrices (wide form) need normalization to row-based xref tables for filtering and joining. (See existing planning notes on crosstab-to-xref.)

*Goal*::
Provide `make_crosstab_to_xref_step` to convert matrix-style sheets into row-based references, preserving optional header conditions.

*Rationale*::
Normal form is easier to query, diff, validate, and compose with other steps.

*Acceptance*

- Configurable row keys, column keys, header rows, marker semantics.
- Optionally drop empty rows (`drop_false=true`).
- Roundtrip examples in tests.

===== FTR-DEMO-AUTOSYNC — Automated dependency update and demo verification

*Purpose:*::
After the demo and library have stabilized, automate version tracking so the demo repo stays current with released library versions without manual intervention.

*Scope:*::
Applies to the public demo repository and optionally to the main project CI configuration.

*Solution:*

- Configure a Dependabot or Renovate workflow that monitors PyPI for new releases of `spreadsheet-handling`.
- Automatically open a pull request in the demo repo updating the version pin in `requirements.txt` or `pyproject.toml`.
- Trigger the demo’s CI pipeline to execute its smoke tests with the updated dependency.
- Optionally report back status to the main repo (e.g., via badge or webhook).
- Define simple labels and reviewers for quick acceptance or rollback.

*Acceptance:*

- New core releases automatically trigger a dependency-update PR in the demo repo within 24 h.
- Demo CI runs successfully against the new version before merge.
- Manual merges remain possible when larger refactors are needed, but routine updates require no manual work.
- Documentation briefly explains the automated update flow and how to pause or override it.

===== FTR-DOMAIN-CONSOLIDATION — Fold scattered domain code into a tidy layer

*Purpose:*::
Simplify the domain by consolidating partially disconnected packages into a single, well-scoped domain module with clear boundaries to adapters and IR.

*Scope:*::
Domain-only; no adapter behavior changes. Requires a coverage gate before refactor to protect functionality.

*Solution:*

- Establish a **coverage floor** (e.g., 80% domain, 70% overall) and add a CI gate.
- Identify public domain API (functions, data types) and mark the rest internal.
- Merge/relocate `core`/`pk` into `domain/` with subpackages `model`, `transformations`, `validation`.
- Provide deprecation shims (`from domain.old import X` → warnings) for one release.

*Acceptance:*

- CI passes with new coverage gate; public API unchanged (or documented with deprecation warnings).
- Imports from the old packages emit a deprecation warning and still work for one cycle.
- Docs show the new domain layout; internal modules are not referenced from examples.
- No adapter/router changes needed; roundtrip tests remain green.
- Packages, `core` / `pk` are gone (or restructures so they take a role in the domain)./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-FORMULA-PROVIDERS.adoc

===== FTR-IR-SHIM-CLEANUP — Remove temporary compatibility shims from new adapters

*Purpose:*::
During the IR refactor several temporary shims (e.g., `render_plan` → `render_workbook`) were introduced to keep legacy tests green.
This feature removes or consolidates those aliases once the test suite and consuming code are fully migrated.

*Scope:*::
Affects functions and symbols within active IR-based backends (not legacy adapters).
Targets files such as `io_backends/xlsx/openpyxl_renderer.py` and related IR renderer modules.

*Solution:*::
- Identify all temporary aliases and `Deprecated:` markers in IR and rendering layers.
- Replace external references with the canonical API.
- Delete the shims and update `__all__` lists.
- Adjust test imports accordingly.

*Acceptance:*::
- No references to deprecated symbols remain in code or tests.
- CI passes with shims removed.
- CHANGELOG and docs mention cleaned-up canonical names.

*Extention for tidy up in context of other FTRs:*::
* *FTR-IR-WRITEPATH-P1*
** Scope:
*** XLSX renderer drops legacy IR `.sheets` acceptance; canonical input is RenderPlan (`.ops`).
*** Remove temporary aliases (e.g., `render_plan(...)`) after callers use `render_workbook(plan, ...)`.
*** Keep adapter interfaces stable from the router outward.
** Acceptance
*** No code path in io_backends.* calls the renderer with IR `.sheets`.
*** `render_workbook` rejects non-Plan objects with a clear TypeError.
*** Test suite passes with Plan-only renderer; deprecation shims deleted../docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-IR-TYPING-CANONICAL.adoc
===== FTR-IR-TYPING-CANONICAL — Replace duck-typed interfaces with typed contracts

*Purpose:*::
Ensure all IR-related components use canonical, type-safe interfaces instead of duck-typed objects. This builds on the shim cleanup (FTR-IR-SHIM-CLEANUP) and enforces clear contracts across the renderer, pipeline, and adapters.

*Scope:*::
- Introduce formal `Protocol`/dataclass definitions for key IR constructs (`RenderPlan`, `RenderStep`, `RenderWorkbook`).
- Update renderer, router, and tests to require these types explicitly instead of inferring shape at runtime.
- Add static type validation (mypy/pyright) to CI and enforce at least one strict-mode run.
- Adjust integration and test fixtures to provide canonical plan objects.

*Acceptance:*::
- All renderer and adapter entry points accept/return declared IR types only.
- No remaining `isinstance`/`hasattr` duck-type checks.
- CI includes type-checking job; mypy passes with zero errors.
- Downstream libraries and demo repos compile cleanly under strict type checking.

*Extension (cleanup from FTR-IR-WRITEPATH-P1):*::
During the IR migration, `TableBlock` temporarily accepted a `top_left` alias to keep legacy tests compatible with older fixture data.
As part of this feature, remove that alias and enforce canonical positional attributes (`top`, `left`) only.
Deprecation warnings may be introduced in one intermediate release before complete removal.

*Acceptance for cleanup:*::
- `TableBlock` no longer defines or accepts the `top_left` argument.
- All tests and fixtures use canonical `top` / `left` initialization.
- No `DeprecationWarning` emitted in strict CI mode.
- Document the change in `CHANGELOG` under “Removed legacy constructor aliases”.

===== FTR-META-BOOTSTRAP — Meta Bootstrap and Fault Tolerance

*Context:*::
Workbooks without persisted meta must still roundtrip. All backends should treat missing meta as `{}` and continue.

*Goal:*::
Provide an early domain step (`bootstrap_meta`) that merges configuration inputs into runtime meta, ensuring deterministic defaults even when persisted meta is missing.+
+
Example for step options are: (e.g., frames.meta.constraints, style.auto_filter, style.freeze_header, style.header_fill_rgb) as we include new features we might have to extend


*Rationale:*::
Prevents `None`-handling errors and gives IR / passes a stable contract without requiring stored meta.

*Precedence Model:*::
Configuration that affects meta may come from several sources. They are applied in the following order (later overwrites earlier unless a step explicitly merges):

. **Persistence:**  Load existing meta from storage if present; otherwise start with `{}`.
. **Pipeline Profile Defaults:**  Apply defaults defined in the selected profile.
. **CLI / Runtime Arguments:**  Overlay any values passed via CLI flags or explicit step configuration. CLI always wins over profile defaults.
. **Step-Local Behavior:**  Individual steps may choose to *merge* instead of overwrite (e.g., appending to lists of non-essential columns). Such merge semantics are step-specific features, not global rules.

Example — Helper Columns:

- Helper columns are marked in meta as non-essential so they can be safely dropped.
- A later step that adds new helpers should append to that list, not replace it.


*Acceptance:*

- Missing meta is treated as `{}` by all backends.
- `bootstrap_meta` merges sources according to the precedence model above.
- IR receives the fully merged meta and renders consistently across runs.

===== FTR-MULTIHEADER-P2 — IR Renderer “Parity Slice v2” (P2) Multi-row/column headers (with merges) + Optional Flattening at I/O

*Purpose:*::
Use pandas MultiIndex headers as the single in-memory standard. JSON/XML may emit nested objects by default; provide an optional edge step to flatten/unflatten when a flat representation is needed (including spreadsheets).

*Scope:*::
Applies to all tabular frames; domain/IR stay MultiIndex. Flattening is an optional **edge step** (Frames→Frames) that can be placed before adapters.

*Context:*::
Slice P2 of the Roadmap towards IR Parity <<RM-IR-PARITY: Parity between IR renderer and legacy renderer, RM-IR-PARITY>>

*Solution:*

* Keep MultiIndex headers canonical in domain/IR.
* Spreadsheet renderer honors `headers.mode`:
  - `multi`: render merged multi-row/col headers with correct data offsets and styles.
  - `flat`: consume pre-flattened frames (produced by the edge step) and render single-line headers.
* JSON/XML adapters: default to nested objects from MultiIndex; accept already-flattened frames from the edge step if configured.
* Provide pure pipeline steps: `flatten_headers(mode=join|first_nonempty, sep='.')` and `unflatten_headers(sep='.')` for reversible mapping.
* Document edge cases (non-unique tuples, empty labels, both-axis levels) and the required conventions (placeholders, coercion, `sep`).

*Acceptance:*

* Domain always operates on MultiIndex headers.
* XLSX: merges when `mode=multi`; renders single-row headers when fed flattened frames.
* JSON/XML: nested output by default; flat output achievable by inserting the flatten step.
* `flatten_headers`/`unflatten_headers` are pure and **lossless** under documented conventions (unique tuples, stable level order, defined `sep`).
* Tests cover: multi→xlsx (merged), multi→json (nested), multi→flatten→xlsx/json (flat), and round-trips with `unflatten_headers`../docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-NAMED-RANGES.adoc

./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-NESTED-LISTS.adoc
===== FTR-NESTED-LISTS — Extract and Recompose Nested Lists from Hierarchical JSON

*Purpose:*::
Enable roundtripping between hierarchical JSON structures (objects containing lists of objects) and tabular frames suitable for spreadsheet or CSV representation.

*Scope:*::
Applies to adapters handling hierarchical formats (JSON, XML). Lists are extracted into separate frames, preserving 1-to-many and nested relationships through synthetic foreign keys.

*Solution:*

* Introduce a transformation step `normalize_nested_lists(frames, meta)` that:
  - Scans JSON-derived frames for columns containing lists of objects or primitives.
  - Emits new frames for each list field (e.g., `orders.items` → frame `orders__items`).
  - Propagates parent identifiers into child frames to preserve referential integrity.
* Provide the inverse `compose_nested_lists(frames, meta)` to re-embed child tables into their parent JSON objects during export.
* Handle recursive/nested lists by repeating the pattern with deterministic naming (`__` or configurable separator).
* Capture the mapping manifest in `meta` for traceability (parent→child frame map).

*Acceptance:*

- JSON with nested lists can be unpacked into multiple tables and re-composed without information loss.
- Each emitted table includes a parent-ID column referencing the originating object.
- Roundtrip tests cover simple and multi-level nesting (1-to-many-to-many).
- Spreadsheet outputs show one sheet per extracted list with consistent naming and keys.
- Config allows custom naming templates and maximum recursion depth.

*Notes:*::
For detailed algorithms and examples (key propagation, naming templates, recursive depth control), see *Concept: Normalizing Nested Structures* in Chapter 2.

See <<FTR-JSON-BUNDLER.adoc#, FTR-JSON-BUNDLER>> for the normalization logic.

Depends on: <<FTR-JSON-BUNDLER.adoc#, FTR-JSON-BUNDLER>>
./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-ODS-RENDERER.adoc

*Acceptance*::

- Clear NotImplemented errors; tests ensure graceful selection/fallback.
- Follow-up item for ODS Style/Validation parity.
./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-ONE-ORCHESTRATOR.adoc
===== FTR-008: Orchestrator Unification — Single shared orchestrate(...) for sheets-run, sheets-pack, and sheets-unpack

*Context:*::
Historically, pack/unpack duplicated flow logic. We now prefer a single execution engine and have wrappers construct pipelines.

*Goal:*::
Provide a shared function orchestrate(pipeline=None, profile=None, io_overrides=None, ...) used by all CLIs. sheets-run and the wrappers call this engine instead of delegating CLI→CLI.

*Rationale:*::
One engine removes drift, simplifies testing, and enables reuse in services (e.g., FastAPI) and batch jobs without re-implementing control flow.

*Solution Steps*

* Extract current run-logic into spreadsheet_handling.orchestrator:orchestrate(...) (resolve pipeline/profile, route I/O via backends, apply passes, collect results).
* Make sheets-run parse args → call orchestrate(...) (no extra logic).
* Make sheets-pack/sheets-unpack build their pipelines from flags as today → call orchestrate(pipeline=..., io_overrides=..., ...).
* Keep steps pure (Frames→Frames); ensure router backends own all I/O. Preserve profile override semantics from CLI.
* (Optional) Add a lightweight deprecation note in pack/unpack help pointing users to sheets-run + profiles for advanced flows.

*Acceptance*

- A single module spreadsheet_handling/orchestrator.py exposes orchestrate(...) with a stable signature.
- sheets-run calls orchestrate(...) directly (no CLI-to-CLI delegation).
- sheets-pack and sheets-unpack construct pipelines and then call orchestrate(...).
- Pipelines remain pure; all I/O is handled by the router backends; profiles can override I/O and options.
- Docs show both flag-only and profile-based runs for sheets-run, and wrapper usage that yields identical artifacts.
- Unit tests patch orchestrate and assert it is invoked by all three CLIs with the expected arguments.
- Integration tests confirm outputs are unchanged vs. pre-refactor for representative pack/unpack scenarios.
- The engine is importable and suitable for reuse in a web service without invoking any CLI layer.

===== FTR-PARITY-IR-P3 — IR Renderer Parity with Legacy OpenPyXL

*Context*::
During migration, the IR-backed XLSX renderer must match legacy outputs for core scenarios (style, validations, sheet naming).
A short-lived CI safeguard verifies parity on a controlled set of fixtures while refactors are still landing.

*Goal*::
Achieve parity in layout and key behaviors; provide test fixtures that compare legacy vs IR outputs for selected cases.
Prove correctness under real CI conditions, then prepare to flip to IR-only.

*Rationale*::
Temporary parity verification prevents silent regressions from transitive changes (deps, locale/ordering, shared utils) during the migration window.
Confidence for deprecating legacy path; documents expected equivalence.

*Acceptance*::
* A dedicated CI job **parity-ir** runs a small fixture suite with **both** backends and asserts **normalized structural equivalence** (sheets/order, styles, filters, validations, meta) — not byte-zip equality.
* Job triggers only on:
** Changes under `ir/`, `xlsx/`, `compose/`, `passes/`, CI config, or dependency manifests.
** A nightly run during migration.
* Environment is hardened and pinned in the job: `TZ=UTC`, `LC_ALL=C`, fixed `PYTHONHASHSEED`, pinned Python minor + XLSX deps.
* Parity suite covers (minimum):
** Header styles (bold/fill), AutoFilter, optional freeze first row.
** Validations: in-list and basic numeric (min/max).
** Sheet naming and order.
** Hidden `_meta` sheet with minimal fields (e.g., `version`, `exported_at`, `author`).
* Stability gate: **10 consecutive green runs** across the supported CI matrix over **7 calendar days**, with **zero flakes** recorded.
* Exit outcome of P3: open a prepared PR (or branch) that flips adapters to IR by default and is blocked on P4 acceptance.

IMPORTANT: No product-surface flag: the IR/legacy switch exists **only in tests/CI**; adapters in production code remain unchanged in P3.

*Context:*
Slice P3 of the Roadmap towards IR Parity <<RM-IR-PARITY: Parity between IR renderer and legacy renderer, RM-IR-PARITY>>

===== FTR-ROUNDTRIP-SAFE-P1 — Controlled round-trip for spreadsheet layouts

Purpose:::
Ensure that workbooks produced by our renderer can be edited in a controlled way and then re-imported into the IR/domain without structural drift. The goal is predictable round-tripping for our exported shapes, not arbitrary spreadsheets.

Scope:::
- Define two supported scenarios and their constraints:
** Scenario A — Flat table(s) without named ranges: one or more tables on a sheet, discoverable by start anchors; growth by appending rows/columns until a stopping condition.
** Scenario B — Multiple tables with named ranges: each table is delimited by a named range and can safely co-exist with other tables on the same sheet.
- Define metadata bootstrap strategies for imports with and without embedded meta.
- Provide a minimal parser (parse_ir) that reconstructs a canonical IR from supported layouts.

Design Principles:::
- Stable anchors over heuristics: prefer explicit coordinates or named ranges to infer boundaries.
- Explicit meta over guessing: when available, embedded meta (_meta sheet or named meta range) wins over heuristics.
- Controlled edit surface: allow appending rows, inserting columns inside table ranges, and editing values; disallow structural ops that break anchors (e.g., merges over headers) unless covered in a later phase.
- Lossless data, lossy style: guarantee round-trip for data and metadata; styling may be normalized.

Supported Scenarios (P1):::
.Scenario A — Flat tables
 - Each table has a start anchor (top-left cell).
 - Table grows down/right until the first fully empty row/column (stop sentinel).
 - Guideline: Prefer one table per sheet in A to avoid accidental cross-contamination when users insert empty rows/columns. If multiple tables are needed, strongly consider Scenario B.

.Scenario B — Multi-table with named ranges
 - Each table is defined by a named range (e.g., tbl_customers, tbl_orders).
 - Ranges strictly define the import/export area.
 - Writer ensures named range creation; reader resolves tables by names.

Metadata Bootstrap (when importing):::
Order of precedence to discover structure:
 1) Embedded meta (hidden _meta sheet or named range __sh_meta) → JSON/YAML with table ids, range names, and typing.
 2) Named ranges (Scenario B).
 3) Anchors config (Scenario A) provided via CLI/args (e.g., --tables S!A1, --tables S!A1,S!J1).
 4) Sidecar file (workbook.xlsx.meta.json) colocated with the file.
 5) Heuristics fallback (discouraged): first non-empty header row + sentinel empties; can be disabled by flag.

CLI & Pipeline Extensions:::
- New optional flags for the import step:
 * --meta-source=embedded|sidecar|none
 * --table=Sheet1!A1[:NamedRange] (repeatable)
 * --stop-on-empty-row / --stop-on-empty-col (Scenario A controls)
- In pipeline YAML, mirror the same options.

Implementation Sketch:::
- parse_ir(xlsx_path, options) -> WorkbookIR
 * Reads embedded meta (if present) and resolves tables.
 * If Scenario B, enumerate named ranges and materialize table blocks.
 * If Scenario A, use provided anchors + sentinel rules.
 * Populate IR with blocks, headers, data, validations (where resolvable).
- Renderer continues to write _meta and named ranges.

Acceptance:::
- Given a workbook produced by our renderer:
 * Edits limited to appending rows, inserting columns within a table range, and changing values are round-trip safe.
 * parse_ir reconstructs the same logical table set (ids, order, and shapes) for both Scenario A and B.
- A test fixture set covers A (single-table per sheet) and B (multi-table with named ranges).
- Docs include a 'How to edit safely' section.

Out of Scope (P1):::
- Complex merges in headers (covered by Multi-header/P2).
- Arbitrary user-inserted shapes/charts/pivots.
- Structural changes that shift anchors without meta updates.

References:::
- Concept <<_concept_ftr_roundtrip_safe_p1_round_trip_strategy_for_spreadsheet_layouts,Round Trip Strategy for Spreadsheets with Layouts>>./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-STYLE-THEMES.adoc

===== FTR-VALIDATION-COMPACT — Compact code validation generator (with cap)

*Context*::
Large in-list validations degrade Excel UX and can exceed limits.

*Goal*::
Provide a configurable cap (e.g., default 200) beyond which the renderer skips list-materialization and logs a warning.

*Rationale*::
Balances usability with technical constraints.

**Solution design**

* Generate allowed dropdown values as all presence/absence combinations across participating layers (order preserved),
with a cap (e.g., 200) to avoid unusable Excel lists.
* concrete cap value can receive override via config
* explicit validations can be given (e.g. via a generic validation feature already in place) - in this case the heuristic is not applied

*Acceptance*::

- lists generated; capped with clear warning; applied via DataValidation.
- `excel.validation_cap` default applied; per-sheet override possible.
- Above cap: fallback to free text (no list) with log warning.
- Unit tests assert cap behavior.

*Depends-on*::
FTR-COMPACT-TRANSFORMS./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/open/FTR-VALIDATION-PASS-INFRA.adoc

./docs/internal_guide/backlog/ftrs/roadmaps/RM-IR-PARITY.adoc
===== RM-IR-PARITY: Parity between IR renderer and legacy renderer

We are refactoring the spreadsheet-facing backends, which were initially called directly by the domain layer, to route through an intermediate representation (IR).
The roadmap defines progressive slices toward functional parity, CI-proven stability, and final deprecation of the legacy OpenPyXL path.

* *P1 — IR Parity Slice v1 (current)*
- *Feature:* <<FTR-IR-WRITEPATH-P1 — IR write pipeline with openpyxl renderer: “Parity Slice v1” (P1) and wire CI around it,FTR-IR-WRITEPATH-P1>>
- *Scope:* Header style + AutoFilter + optional freeze row, simple in-list validations, sheet names/order, minimal meta sheet.
- *Outcome:* Small parity suite runs in CI under `SH_XLSX_BACKEND=ir`; legacy renderer remains default elsewhere.

* *Shim Cleanup — Remove temporary IR compatibility shims*
- *Feature:* <<FTR-IR-SHIM-CLEANUP — Remove temporary compatibility shims from new adapters,FTR-IR-SHIM-CLEANUP>>
- *Scope:*
** Remove or consolidate transitional aliases (`render_plan`, `render_workbook`).
** Ensure all adapters and tests use canonical `RenderPlan` entry points only.
** Adjust imports, delete deprecated symbols, and confirm CI passes without shims.
- *Outcome:* IR path free of transitional glue; only canonical API names remain.

* *P2 — IR Parity Slice v2: Multi-headers & merges*
- *Feature:* <<FTR-MULTIHEADER-P2 — IR Renderer “Parity Slice v2” (P2) Multi-row/column headers (with merges) + Optional Flattening at I/O,FTR-MULTIHEADER-P2>>
- *Scope:* 2D header blocks, horizontal/vertical merges, optional flattening during read/write (configurable), parity fixtures for typical 2–3 level headers.

* *P2.5 — IR Round-trip Safe (Controlled Read Path)*

- *Feature:* <<FTR-ROUNDTRIP-SAFE-P1 — Controlled round-trip for spreadsheet layouts,FTR-ROUNDTRIP-SAFE-P1>>
- *Purpose:* Establish a predictable, metadata-driven **read path** for spreadsheets created by the IR renderer.
- *Scope:*
** Implement a parser (`parse_ir`) that reconstructs an IR from structured XLSX files written by our renderer.
** Support two controlled editing modes:
*** *Scenario A* — Flat tables (single or adjacent) discovered by anchor position and stop sentinel.
*** *Scenario B* — Multiple tables defined by named ranges.
** Introduce a metadata bootstrap hierarchy (embedded `_meta` sheet → named ranges → CLI args → sidecar file).
** Define and document which user edits are round-trip safe (append rows, insert columns, edit data values).
** Write fixtures and regression tests covering both A and B, verifying round-trip parity (write → edit → read).
- *Outcome:*
** The IR layer becomes bidirectional (render + parse).
** Data and metadata round-trip safely under defined edit constraints.
** Style remains lossy but deterministic.
** Provides a foundation for later test harness and parity verification phases.
- *Relations:*
** Builds on `FTR-IR-WRITEPATH-P1` and `FTR-MULTIHEADER-P2`.
** Enables `FTR-TEST-HARNESS` and future end-to-end CI parity checks.
** Informs later cleanup work under `FTR-IR-TYPING-CANONICAL` and `FTR-CLEANUP-IR-P4`.

* *P3 — IR Parity Slice v3: Parity Verification & Temporary CI Safeguard*
- *Feature:* <<FTR-PARITY-IR-P3 — IR Renderer Parity with Legacy OpenPyXL,FTR-PARITY-IR-P3>>
- *Scope:*
** Establish a short-lived CI job (`parity-ir`) that compares IR vs. legacy outputs on a fixed fixture set.
** Triggered only on relevant paths or nightly; runs in pinned, reproducible environment.
** Ensures parity in layout, style, validations, and metadata persistence.
** Stability gate (e.g., 10 consecutive green runs across matrix) unlocks IR default activation.
** No product-surface flags — safeguard limited to CI/testing only.
- *Outcome:* Verified confidence that IR renderer behavior matches legacy across representative workbooks; IR path ready to become default.

* *P4 — IR Parity Slice v4: Cleanup and Forward-Only Migration*
- *Feature:* <<FTR-CLEANUP-IR-P4 — Remove Legacy Renderer and Parity Safeguard,FTR-CLEANUP-IR-P4>>
- *Scope:*
** Remove the legacy OpenPyXL renderer and all associated flags, code paths, and Make targets.
** Delete the temporary `parity-ir` CI job and convert fixtures to IR-only golden snapshot tests.
** Finalize IR as the sole backend; close out `docs/legacy_gap.md`.
** Release notes mark removal of the legacy path and completion of IR migration.
- *Outcome:* Clean, single-path IR renderer implementation with no fallback or CI safeguard remaining.

* *FTR-IR-TYPING-CANONICAL — Replace duck-typed interfaces with typed contracts*
- *Purpose:* Consolidate typing once the shim cleanup is done and IR-only paths are stable.
- *Scope:*
** Replace ad-hoc duck typing in renderer and backend interfaces with `Protocol` or concrete dataclass types (`RenderPlan`, `RenderStep`, `RenderWorkbook`).
** Add type enforcement via mypy/pyright CI checks and static contract tests.
** Ensure serialization and adapter boundaries remain type-safe.
- *Outcome:* Canonical, statically typed IR interfaces; maintainability and IDE support improved; duck-typed compatibility paths fully removed.

-> Confidence to deprecate the legacy path and complete the IR migration.

NOTE: A short-lived parity CI job is best practice for compiler/renderer migrations when refactors and dependency updates are still in motion. Use **only** during active migration; plan removal immediately after the stability gate.

Roadmaps describe chains of features (FTRs) that build upon each other. These chains may cut across epics. The roadmaps are supposed to provide long term guidance and context.

'''

=== Project Status Notice

*Spreadsheet-Handling* is an **early beta** project.

- Current public version: pre-release on PyPI (0.1.x-beta).
- Primary user and maintainer: internal
- No external adoption known at this point; interfaces may change without deprecation periods.
- The focus is on establishing clean architecture, test coverage, and documentation rather than release cadence.
- Structural refactors and feature deprecations are permitted freely until the first stable release (≥ 1.0.0).
- Compatibility guarantees will start only once the domain and adapter layers have stabilized.

*Implication for planning:*  Features marked as *deprecated* or *to-be-merged* can be removed without migration work.  All roadmap phases (1–4) are internal milestones only and may be reordered as the design evolves.

*API Evolution Policy (Beta)*::

Minor renames and structural refactors are allowed, but every public-facing API change
(domain, adapter, or renderer) should either:
- update all internal callers within the same change set, or
- introduce a short-lived compatibility shim marked `# Deprecated` and schedule its removal in the next FTR-CLEANUP phase.

Frequent spontaneous renames without tracking create technical debt; therefore,
changes to stable module boundaries (e.g., io_backends.*, rendering.*) should be
recorded through an FTR entry../docs/internal_guide/backlog/_backlog.adoc
